[HEADLINE] :  jury rules for clint eastwood
[TEXT]
san  jose, calif. (ap) -- clint eastwood was cast as the villain
but  considered himself the hero. in the end, a federal jury saw
things  his way.
eastwood  was cleared friday of having to pay damages to a
disabled  woman who sued him because his historic inn near carmel
lacked  wheelchair access. the jury deliberated less than five hours
in  siding with eastwood, who claimed he had been set up.
''i  think there were too many lies told in court and i think the
jury  could see through that,'' eastwood said shortly before he
thanked  the jurors, signed autographs for them and let court
marshals  take pictures with him.
the  plaintiff, 51-year-old diane zum brunnen, who has muscular
dystrophy,  was not in court when the verdict was read. her
attorneys  said they were considering an appeal and said eastwood's
celebrity  status influenced the jury.
zum  brunnen sued eastwood under the americans with disabilities
act  in 1997, a year after she and her husband, michael, say they
had  dinner at mission ranch. the couple from alameda complained
that  the wheelchair-accessible bathroom was in another building,
more  than 200 feet away, across a driveway; the only accessible
guest  room was $225 a night, when other rooms were as low as $85;
and  there was no ramp to the main office.
after  a seven-day trial, the jury found eastwood liable for two
minor  violations: not enough signs to the restroom and no ramp
access  to the hotel office. but they said zum brunnen deserved
nothing  in damages.
eastwood  had contended that zum brunnen and her husband didn't
eat  dinner at the ranch on jan. 21, 1996, as they claimed, but
instead  stopped by to snap a quick picture of the office they could
use  in a lawsuit.
the  picture was taken some distance from the office, with cars
in  the foreground, on a sunny day.
the  zum brunnens said in depositions they took the picture after
dinner  -- when it would have been dark -- but said at trial it was
taken  before dinner.
a  surveyor testified that the picture was taken at 12:05 p.m.,
which  apparently convinced the jurors that the zum brunnens'
stories  had holes.
''we  kind of didn't think she was really there for dinner,''
said  juror lorenzo gutierrez, 37.
zum  brunnen's attorneys admitted there were inconsistencies but
chalked  that up to the passage of time, rather than a failed
conspiracy  to nail eastwood. the zum brunnens' phone number is
unlisted;  they could not be reached for comment.
eastwood,  a former mayor of carmel, said he has tried to provide
disabled  access in his renovations to the 150-year-old ranch, which
he  bought in 1987, while preserving the inn's historic feel.
''i'm  not against the ada; i want to make that clear,'' he said.
though  zum brunnen's side portrayed the case as a simple fight
for  a disabled woman's civil rights, it was impossible to ignore
the  70-year-old eastwood's role. both sides accused the other of
seeking  a ''fistful of dollars'' -- a reference to his 1964 western.
eastwood  was asked outside court if this would have been the
verdict  he would have scripted had the case been a movie.
''as  a matter of fact,'' he said, smiling, ''it's not a bad
ending,  is it?''

[HEADLINE] :  fina suspends italian coach
[TEXT]
sydney,  australia (ap) -- international water polo officials have
suspended  italy's coach ratko rudic a year from any fina events for
his  angry display after his team lost to hungary in the olympic
quarterfinals.
 fina  officials met at the sydney international aquatic center on
saturday.  in a statement, they said that rudic was disciplined for
''having  brought the sport of water polo in disrepute.''
rudic,  who won golds with yugoslavia in 1984 and 1988 and with
italy  in 1992, chased the officials after the game and was arguing
so  loudly a uniformed officer stepped between him and the scorer's
table  at the ryde aquatic leisure center.
in  a post-game conference, rudic accused officials of conspiring
against  his team. ''i have no proof,'' he said through an
interpreter.  he said the conspiracy might have been held through
secret  meetings. ''it's too sophisticated for me,'' he said.
italy  appealed the game on a technical error and asked it be
replayed,  but it was denied by fina.
rudic  is not expected to be at italy's games the rest of the
olympics.
 also,  fina suspended three italian players for their conduct in
slamming  the pooldeck and arguing with officials following friday's
loss.
 roberto  calcaterra was suspended for four international games.
his  brother, alessandro, was suspended for two games and goalie
francisco  attolico was suspended a game.

an  official after his team fell to spain, 9-8. simenc pointed and
yelled  at an official once the game ended.

[HEADLINE] :  u.s. men to play france for gold
[TEXT]
sydney,  australia (ap) -- does france have a chance?
even  the french players didn't think so after they beat
australia  to reach the gold medal game, but now all bets are off
after  the american men had a huge scare in the semifinals.
''right  now france is our toughest game,'' coach rudy
tomjanovich  said.
on  friday night, lithuania provided a tougher test than anybody
would  have ever imagined. no more than three points separated the
teams  over the final 15&amp;frac12; minutes and the game wasn't decided until
the  final shot -- a 3-pointer by sarunas jasikevicius -- was
off-target  at the final buzzer.
the  final score of 85-83 represented the closest game for an
american  men's team in the olympics since 1988 -- the final year
that  collegians represented the united states.
''we  were fighting for our lives,'' ray allen said. ''it would
not  have been very fun to play for the bronze medal. but these
teams  are good, and we know that on sunday we could be in the same
situation  if we don't come out and just play the game of
basketball.''
 aside  from friday night's near-miracle, the surprise of the last
few  days of the tournament has been france. after finishing fourth
in  group a to barely make it to the medal round, the french rolled
past  canada, the first place team in group b, and then knocked off
the  host team, australia, with ease.
the  french players hugged each other and celebrated after
beating  the aussies like they had won the gold medal, knowing in
the  back of their minds that they really have no chance to beat the
americans.  a few hours later, they may have been reconsidering
their  earlier thoughts
''i  just wanted to get the silver medal, so i played my best,''
france  center frederic weis said.
could  there be another surprise in store?
''i  don't know if it's possible,'' weis said, ''but we'll see. a
game  is a game, so we'll try.''
france  scored 94 points against the americans in the preliminary
round  and lost by just 12 in a game that was highlighted by vince
carter  soaring over the head of the 7-foot-2 weis for an incredible
slam  dunk.
''am  i the first guy he dunked against?'' weis asked friday,
laughing  at his own humor.
france  will look to get most of its offense from guards laurent
sciarra  and antoine rigaudeau, both of whom are a threat from
3-point  range.
rigaudeau  is shooting 37 percent from 3-point range in the
olympics  and is averaging a team-high 13.0 points per game, while
sciarra  has shot 42.3 percent from 3-point range while averaging
10.1  points per game. weis is their leading rebounder, and guard
makan  dioumassi is their defensive stopper off the bench.
france's  third-leading scorer, yann bonato, ruptured his
achilles  tendon against canada and has already returned home.
''since  we played well in our loss to the united states we have
lost  all our inhibitions,'' france coach jean pierre de vincenzi
said.  ''we are happy. we have to be. this has not happened for us
since  1948.''
the  americans, meanwhile, were feeling a huge sense of relief
saturday  after avoiding what would have been one of the biggest
upsets  in the history of basketball, olympics or otherwise.
unable  to create turnovers with their pressure defense and
unable  to pull away from the no-quit lithuanians, the u.s. team was
further  flummoxed by lithuania's use of a tight 2-3 zone defense.
the  americans repeatedly pounded the ball inside, where they were
quickly  double-teamed, and were often unsuccessful trying to shoot
over  the zone from 3-point range.
incredibly,  it came down to a final shot that might have come
closer  had jason kidd not been playing such tight defense on
jasikevicius.
 ''i  had a sigh of relief when i saw that the ball didn't touch
anything  and the time had expired off the clock,'' ray allen said.
''it  was a situation we put ourselves in, but when we win the gold
medal  we can definitely say that we earned it.''
first,  however, the americans have to earn it one last time.
tip-off  for the gold medal game is 10 p.m. edt saturday.
lithuania  plays australia in the bronze medal game at 8 p.m.
edt.

[HEADLINE] :  felix savon wins boxing gold
[TEXT]
sydney,  australia (ap) -- felix savon didn't look like a winner,
but  he was. so was cuba, which will go home with its usual olympic
boxing  medal haul.
savon  was bleeding badly from a deep cut under his left eye as
his  fight with russia's sultanahmed ibzagimov drew to an end
saturday.  by that time, though, he had landed his big right hand
enough  to secure his third olympic heavyweight boxing gold.
savon  became only the third boxer to win three olympic gold
medals,  joining former cuban heavyweight teofilo stevenson and
hungary's  lazlo papp as triple gold medalists.
three  of savon's teammates also won gold medal fights, giving
the  powerful cuban team four gold medals -- the same total it won in
atlanta  -- and two bronze.
six  more gold medal bouts will be fought sunday, but no cubans
are  in them. no americans fought saturday, but two are in gold
medal  bouts on sunday.
savon,  who won gold medals in 1992 and 1996 and is a six-time
world  amateur champion, came into the ring with a mark under his
left  eye that appeared swollen from a previous fight.
it  didn't stop him from piling up points against the russian,
who  had trouble getting inside the reach of the 6-foot-6 cuban
heavyweight.  a punch in the fourth round opened a deep cut below
the  eye, but savon was allowed to continue and won 21-13.
as  savon went back to his corner, blood was streaming down his
face  from the cut.
a  few moments later, though, he was happily dancing in the ring,
waving  a cuban flag in victory.
''i'm  really happy. i dedicate this to the people of cuba,''
savon  said.
the  33-year-old savon has dominated amateur heavyweight boxing
for  the last decade, though there were whispers that he was fading
as  he got off to a rocky start in his first fight before beating
his  nigerian opponent.
michael  bennett was next for savon, who used his powerful right
hand  to pile up enough points to stop the inexperienced american
late  in the third round.
''he's  a great warrior,'' bennett said.
savon  was cut under the left eye in a semifinal fight he won
over  a german, but was allowed to continue and fight in the gold
medal  bout.
ibzagimov,  who landed some telling blows in the final two
rounds,  said he followed the wrong strategy for the fight.
''i  came out and boxed defensively, and it was a mistake,'' he
said.
 other  cubans winning saturday were ortiz rigondeaux, a
20-year-old  newcomer at 119 pounds, and veterans mario kindelan at
132  pounds and jorge gutierrez at 165 pounds.
the  other two gold medals were won by brahim asloum of france at
106  pounds, and oleg saitov of russia at 147 pounds.
it  was the second olympic gold for saitov, who also won in
atlanta.
 ''i  don't know what i'm going to do now,'' saitov said after
beating  sergei dotsenko of the ukraine, 24-16. ''i don't like
planning  ahead. i will just let things happen.''
saitov's  win brightened the day for the russian team, which came
into  the finals with the most boxers still in the competition --
five  -- but lost three of four fights.
the  first boxing gold went to asloum, who earlier in the
tournament  had beaten favored brian viloria of the united states at
106  pounds.
asloum  was fighting perhaps the smallest boxer in 4-foot-11
rafael  lozano of spain, who was fighting in his third olympics.
lozano,  who won a bronze medal in atlanta, fought hard but just
couldn't  keep the pressure on asloum, who was wearing his hair in
his  country's colors of white, blue and red.
''i  wanted the gold, but i got the silver. i hope my girlfriend
will  talk to me tonight,'' lozano said.

[HEADLINE] :  cuba beats russia 3-2 in volleyball
[TEXT]
sydney,  australia (ap) -- the cuban women maintained their
volleyball  dominance with their greatest olympic triumph.
rallying  from a two-game deficit, cuba stormed back to win a
record  third consecutive gold medal with a thrilling 25-27, 32-34,
25-19,  25-18, 15-7 victory over russia saturday.
''we  are cubans. we came here to do the best, and that meant
fighting  until the end,'' captain regla bell said.
cuba  now has won every major international competition since the
1992  games, building an amazing 35-3 record in world championships
and  olympics.
the  difference in ability and execution between the two teams
was  minuscule, and they battled back and forth in a match befitting
the  sport's two superpowers.
cuba  had a 24-21 lead in the opener before letting it slip away.
in  the second game, cuba led 24-23 but again failed to close. both
teams  fought for and lost four more game points until russia pulled
ahead  33-32 on a kill by elena godina, who then closed it out by
stuffing  marlenis costa at the net.
regla  torres, cuba's greatest player, brought her team back by
getting  her 6-foot-3 frame into the path of the russian players as
often  as possible.
''we  were very tense in the first two sets, because of the
pressure  of winning a third gold medal,'' torres said. ''then we
relaxed  and changed the way we played.''
torres,  who became the youngest volleyball gold medalist when
she  played on the 1992 team at age 17, was fearless in the middle,
attacking  the 6-4 godina and russia's other main scoring threat,
6-3  liobov chachkova.
cuba  jumped to a 20-9 lead in the fourth game and withstood a
late  rally. in the deciding game, the cubans took an 8-4 lead and
kept  hitting, as the young russian team folded.
torres  got the final kill, a shot from the right side.
''these  last few games have been the most difficult of my
career,''  torres said. ''this has been one of those achievements i
won't  forget in all my life. i dedicate this win to the whole
country  of cuba. i hope it will be an inspiration to the women of
cuba.''
 the  victory was sweet for cuban coach luis calderon. he had
replaced  eugenio george, the national team coach for 15 years,
after  george left the program in a dispute with sports officials.
fiery  russian coach nikolai karpol, meanwhile, fumed to the very
end.
 karpol,  who led the soviet union to gold medals in 1980 and
1988,  had become the most-booed man among the crowds at sydney
entertainment  center with his fist-shaking tirades against his
players.  as the cubans celebrated, he argued with officials over a
previous  call.
karpol  was under intense pressure to bring home a winner after
the  team's fourth-place finish in atlanta. russia had won four
golds  and three silvers since volleyball became a medal sport in
1964.  besides 1996, the only time the russians had not finished
first  or second was in 1984, when the nation boycotted the los
angeles  games.

[HEADLINE] :  reynolds sails to second gold medal
[TEXT]
sydney,  australia (ap) -- mark reynolds stood barefoot on the
dock,  an american flag in his left hand, and marveled at how he won
his  second olympic sailing gold medal.
his  victory on the pacific ocean on saturday (friday night edt)
was  just the latest example of why the 44-year-old san diego
sailmaker  has been called the star of the star class.
''it  is great to have come from behind,'' said reynolds, a
four-time  olympian. ''there were probably a few people that counted
us  out after six races.
''i  won't say that i counted myself out, but at that point i was
starting  to be concerned more about getting into the medals than
just  worrying about a gold.''
after  a slow start in this regatta, reynolds and his crew,
magnus  liljedahl, 46, of miami, rallied and were assured of at
least  the bronze medal when the day began.
that's  what it looked like they would get after going over the
starting  line early in the 11th and deciding fleet race, the
combination  of aggressiveness and being trapped there by gavin
brady,  a new zealander who lives in america.
reynolds  had to turn back and cross the starting line again.
instead  of being buried in the 16-boat fleet, he ended up gaining
from  a wind shift on the right side of the course, while most
everyone  else thought the first shift would come on the left side.
''we  decided to really go for it at the start and unfortunately,
i  get a little too wound up and we kind of went over everybody and
we  were over the line,'' said reynolds, who also is the current
star  world champion.
reynolds  had enough speed to loop back around and not have that
bad  of a start on port tack, with clear air.
''we  were really fortunate because the right side was a little
favored,''  he said. ''we got a little bit of a shift, and as soon
as  we got that, bang, we tacked back and we knew we were in the
pack,  we knew we had a chance.''
reynolds  rounded the buoy at the top of the windward first leg
in  second place, which, as it turned out, was gold medal position.
he  finished second behind canada's ross macdonald, holding off
britain  skipper ian walker by one point for the gold.
walker  worked his way up to finish third in the final race.
reynolds  and walker came into the race tied for second on points.
defending  star gold medalist torben grael of brazil came in with
a  five-point lead. he was disqualified for being over the line
early  and not turning back to restart, but still got the bronze,
his  fourth olympic medal.
in  the america's cup earlier this year, grael served as
tactician  aboard italy's luna rossa, which was swept by new zealand
in  the finals.
reynolds'  gold helps restore some glitter to the american
sailing  team, which was embarrassed in its home waters in savannah,
ga.,  in 1996 by winning just two bronzes. four years earlier at
barcelona,  the united states won medals in nine of 10 classes,
including  the gold won by reynolds and his crew, hal haenel.
reynolds  won the gold in '92 with one race left to sail. this
time,  he needed all 11 races.
''we  had unbelievable luck in '92,'' reynolds said. ''this was a
lot  more difficult.''
reynolds,  who owns a sail loft near the san diego yacht club,
won  the silver medal in 1988. he is a second-generation star sailor
and  protege of dennis conner.
his  father, jim, who won a star world championship with conner
and  fell just short in three attempts to make it to the olympics,
was  among several family members watching from south head.
reynolds  sailed into the top three with three strong finishes on
friday,  including a first.
he  was assured of a medal in an off-the-water development.
bermuda's  peter bromby sought and received redress for a breakdown
that  kept him from starting one of friday's races, but bromby's
adjusted  score wasn't enough to give him a shot at a medal.
the  deciding race was sailed in moderate breeze and heavy swells
off  the cliffs of the sydney heads.

[HEADLINE] :  4 palestinians dead following clash
[TEXT]
jerusalem  (ap) -- israeli riot police stormed a major jerusalem
shrine  friday and opened fire on stone-throwing muslim worshippers,
killing  four palestinians and wounding 175 in the worst bloodshed
in  four years at the walled compound at the center of the deadlock
in  mideast peace talks.
forty-four  police officers, including the jerusalem chief, were
hit  by stones. the violence quickly spread to jerusalem
neighborhoods  and the west bank, further dimming prospects for an
israeli-palestinian  peace treaty.
the  palestinian authority accused the israeli government of
having  ignited a ''religious war'' and called for a general strike
and  a day of mourning in the palestinian areas saturday. israeli
officials  said they were trying to cool the situation. peace talks
have  been stalled since july over the issue of sovereignty over the
shrines.
 violence  flared again saturday, as hundreds of palestinians
threw  stones at israeli soldiers outside the jewish settlement of
kfar  darom in the gaza strip. israeli troops responded with rubber
bullets.  there was no immediate word on injuries.
tension  has been running high since thursday, when the hawkish
israeli  opposition leader, ariel sharon, toured the jerusalem
shrine,  revered by muslims and jews, to demonstrate that israel is
in  control.
friday's  violence began after muslim noon prayers when the
compound  was filled with 20,000 worshippers. several hundred
palestinians  began hurling stones at israeli riot police huddling
behind  plexiglas shields at the compound's moghrabi gate. officers
fired  barrages of rubber-coated steel pellets and snipers shot live
rounds.  police, many wielding clubs, then charged, chasing
stone-throwers.
 in  the mayhem, palestinian protesters hit by rubber bullets fell
to  the ground and were carried away on stretchers. one young man
was  unconscious, his forehead smeared by blood. others slumped on
the  cobblestone plaza, holding their stomachs and heads in pain.
shouts  of ''allahu akbar,'' or god is great, mixed with the sounds
of  gunfire.
as  news of the clashes spread, riots erupted in other areas of
traditionally  arab east jerusalem and the west bank. in the
biblical  town of bethlehem, rocks littered the main road and thick
clouds  of black smoke from burning tires rose into the skies. one
stone-thrower,  his face covered by a black hood, was taken into a
chokehold  by israeli troops.
by  day's end, four palestinians were dead and at least 175 were
wounded  by rubber bullets and live rounds, most shot in the upper
body,  hospital officials said. forty-four israeli policemen and 15
civilians  were hurt by stones. eight cars, including police vans
and  ambulances, were set on fire or had windshields smashed.
one  of the dead, bilal afani, 26, was a palestinian laborer from
the  west bank suburb of abu dis. before leaving his home friday, he
had  talked about having a party later in the day for his daughter's
first  birthday, said bilal's brother, ahmed.
''i  don't know if i am sad or happy, because my brother gave his
blood  for al aqsa (the main jerusalem mosque), and this is an honor
for  the family,'' said ahmed afani after thousands attended his
brother's  funeral.
the  36-acre walled shrine is known to jews as the temple mount,
site  of their former biblical temple, judaism's holiest site. to
muslims,  it is haram as-sharif, or noble sanctuary, home to two
major  mosques that mark the spot where tradition says the prophet
muhammad  ascended to heaven.
the  palestinian cabinet said after its weekly meeting friday
that  israeli troops opened fire ''without warning and without
justification  in a planned attack, and after the failure of
sharon's  visit.''
as  the clashes raged, sharon defended his visit to the shrine.
''the  state of israel cannot afford that an israeli citizen will
not  be able to visit part of his country, not to speak about the
holiest  place for the jewish people all around the world,'' sharon
told  cnn.
jerusalem's  hawkish mayor, ehud olmert, a member of sharon's
likud  party, accused palestinian security forces of orchestrating
the  violence.
however,  israel's police minister and acting foreign minister,
shlomo  ben-ami, said he believed the riots were spontaneous. ''our
assessment  is that this is largely linked to this visit (by
sharon),''  ben-ami said, adding that neither the palestinian
authority  nor the israeli government had an interest in an
escalation.
 friday's  clashes were preceded by two deadly attacks on israeli
troops.  on wednesday, an israeli soldier was killed in a bomb
attack  in the gaza strip. on friday morning, a palestinian
policeman  opened fire on israeli colleagues patrolling the west
bank  town of qalqiliya, killing one of the israelis.
israel  barred its citizens from entering palestinian-run areas
to  prevent further friction, and israeli prime minister ehud barak
ordered  more police to be deployed in jerusalem. the violence came
at  the start of the jewish new year which ushers in a 10-day period
of  contemplation and prayer.
ben-ami  and arafat spoke separately by phone with u.s. secretary
of  state madeleine albright on friday. ben-ami tried also tried to
reassure  the palestinians, saying israel was not trying to
challenge  the right of muslims to worship at the haram as-sharif.
the  violence came at a time of increased tensions between
israelis  and palestinians, and at a time of deadlock in peace
treaty  talks. the negotiations are hung up because of rival claims
to  sovereignty over the mosque compound. both sides have said they
would  not grant the other sole control. u.s. mediators have floated
compromise  ideas, but none has been accepted by both israel and the
palestinians.

[HEADLINE] :  controversial calls plague taekwondo
[TEXT]
sydney,  australia (ap) -- the last impression the people running
taekwondo  want its olympic debut to leave is that it's just too
korean  for the rest of the world to ever really break into.
but  while the world taekwondo federation took pains to keep that
from  happening, they weren't able to escape a little controversy.
and  perhaps a bit of sour grapes.
to  make sure the nation that created taekwondo -- the ''way of
the  hand and foot'' -- didn't completely dominate the medals, each
country  except host australia was limited to only four athletes in
the  sydney games, where eight golds were contested.
as  a result, the breadth of the competition was better than most
would  have thought.
nearly  50 nations, from austria to venezuela, entered. taekwondo
even  provided vietnam with its first-ever olympic medal -- a silver
for  tran hieu ngan in the women's 57-kilogram class.
even  some traditional rivals were impressed.
''i  watched two days of taekwondo, and i think it is in many
ways  superior to karate,'' said yushiro yagi, head of japan's
olympic  delegation.
but  despite large and very spirited crowds each day, the sport's
debut  was marred by a few bumps.
like  most sports involving judges, the point system posed a
problem.
 charles  bayou, an official with the ivory coast team, said he
was  unhappy about the refereeing. he was so upset that he even wept
during  a match involving ivorian player n'guessan sebastien konan.
konan  lost to mexico's victor manuel estrada garibay by a score
of  7-4 in a repechage match for the bronze medal.
''i  am a little bit disappointed at the results, which were
unfair,''  bayou said. ''i don't know why they did not count
correctly.''
 in  taekwondo, three judges sit around the square fighting area.
when  they believe a competitor has scored a valid kick, they press
a  red or blue button corresponding with the color of the athlete's
headgear.  the athlete with the most points after three three-minute
rounds  is the winner.
unless  the buttons are pressed virtually simultaneously, the
points  won't resgister, however. and there is always room for
dispute  over what constitutes a valid scoring kick.
halfway  through the four-day competition, two unofficial
complaints  were lodged over point disputes, both in bouts that went
in  favor of australians, prompting the world taekwondo federation
to  issue a statement in its own defense.
''the  wtf has placed a top priority on impartiality in order to
present  this first-time medal sport in the best possible light,''
it  said. the statement noted that judges found to make repeated
arbitrary  calls can be suspended for up to four years.
questions  also were raised over whether judges were unnecesarily
hard  on the korean entrants, allegedly because the wtf believes it
would  be better for the sport's future for korea not to be too
dominant.
 but,  with korea doing quite well, those claims are hard to
support.
 with  just one athlete still to compete, korea had won two golds
and  one silver, pretty much as it had expected coming into the
games.

''the  decision could go either way,'' he said. ''our player has
superior  techniques, but could not use them because of his
opponent's  height advantage.''
kim  admitted that the most important thing for korea at these
games  is keeping taekwondo's olympic future alive, not taking home
all  the golds.
''i  don't know if there is any subtle effort by referees to
check  and balance our supremacy in the sport,'' he said. ''but i
agree  that spreading the golds among a variety of countries would
help  promote taekwondo worldwide.''
french  team coach philippe bouedo wrote off the complaints as
mostly  just sour grapes.
''the  refereeing so far has been very good and fair,'' he said.
''when  you lose, you are upset. when you win, you are happy.''

port-au-prince,  haiti (ap) -- they came at dawn, forcing their

had  been deposed by a military coup in 1991.

regime.
 many  of those accused have fled the country and were being tried

panama.  former militia leader emmanuel ''toto'' constant works as a

proceedings  will resume monday.

fraph  -- the front for the advancement and progress of haiti -- which
constant  led.

prevented  the victims' families from retrieving bodies from the

 the  raboteau slayings were part of a series of attacks
undertaken  to break support for aristide, a charismatic slum priest
who  became the caribbean country's first democratically elected
leader  in 1991.
soldiers  and fraph killed at least 3,000 people and maimed
thousands  more before president clinton in 1994 sent 20,000 troops
to  end the bloodshed and halt an exodus of boat people to florida.
aristide  was restored and the army was abolished. aristide was
succeeded  by his hand-picked successor, preval.
under  both men, only a handful of soldiers and militiamen have
been  tried for coup-related crimes and no more than two or three
have  been convicted.
it  took more than three years for haiti's inefficient judicial
system  to prepare the raboteau case.

[HEADLINE] :  panama struggles with future
[TEXT]
panama  city, panama (ap) -- panama has struggled to overcome
drug,  arms and money-laundering problems largely borne of its
location  at the hemisphere's hub. now, panama's neighbors are
tossing  it yet another dilemma to deal with -- their discarded
strongmen.
 panama's  position as a place of transit has always been its
greatest  asset, but some recent arrivals are adding to the
country's  already serious image problem, observers say.
the  most recent arrival, peru's reviled former intelligence
chief,  vladimiro montesinos, is seeking to join other undesirables
already  in exile here. president mireya moscoso has yet to make a
decision  on his asylum request.
''now  we are not only seen as a country that launders money,
traffics  drugs and weapons, but also one that serves as a
retirement  paradise for political scum like montesinos,'' said
miguel  bernal, a former adviser to moscoso.
some  here see the asylum issue as a chance for panama to help
solve  its neighbor's problems. panama has granted asylum in recent
years  to at least three high-profile dictators or strongmen, and by
so  doing defused some tense situations in their home countries.
there  had been rumors a coup could occur in peru were montesinos
to  be denied asylum here.
others  see the montesinos case as an opportunity to lift
panama's  image, battered by questions over whether the country
could  clean up crime or run the canal the united states turned over
to  panama in 1999.
''now  is the right moment, when everyone's focused on panama, to
defend  the country against unjust accusations,'' said former
justice  minister renato periera.
accusations  of crime and insecurity have rained down on panama
in  recent years. for example, u.s. conservatives opposed to the
canal  handover said that leftist guerrillas in neighboring colombia
have  frequently crossed into panama, and sometimes get their guns
here.
 and,  when montesinos jetted up from south america on sunday, he
followed  roughly the same route used by traffickers who ship
colombian  cocaine up through panama to the united states. in a
sense,  other people's problems have quickly become panama's.
the  government has not taken into account the repercussions of
giving  montesinos asylum, said teresa de arias, vice president of
the  country's legislature.
''having  a man like him here could endanger the country,'' de
arias  said. ''given his past, he could be the target of all sorts
of  violence.''
panamanians  stress that they have done a good job running the
canal  in the nine months since the united states left; that they
are  serious about fighting drug trafficking, and don't want the
arms  trade from colombia's civil war to spill over into their
country.
 the  last thing the country needs, in these circumstances, is a
man  like montesinos who many consider a gangster.
the  country's banking sector -- a mainstay of the economy, born
out  of the huge amount of shipping transactions and a lax
regulatory  environment -- is laboring under the specter of being
placed  on the ''black list'' of rogue money-laundering countries by
the  international financial action task force.
montesinos  arrived here just as the country's congress is
debating  stiffer laws against money laundering. ''it's just better
not  to be on such a list,'' said ricardo alba, who is the
government's  point man on the laws.
and  anti-asylum demonstrations have broken out here, protests
not  seen since panama gave asylum to the shah of iran in 1979.
since  then, panama has allowed in haitian dictator raul cedras,
reviled  former ecuadorean president abdala bucaram, and former
guatemalan  president jorge serrano elias, who attempted to seize
absolute  power in his country in 1993.
astrid  wolf, one of about 80 people who gathered in an
anti-asylum  protest in panama city on tuesday, put it in simple
terms.
 ''we're  trying to be somebody on the world stage, but with
people  like this here, we won't get anywhere.''

[TEXT]
	  new york (ap) - up to half of the roughly 538,000 new york
children  enrolled in a federal health care plan are ineligible and
will  be removed from the plan over the next several months, the new
york  times reported saturday.
some  families began receiving notices several weeks ago that
their  children would be removed from the children's health
insurance  program as early as sunday and that they must apply for
medicaid,  the newspaper said.
health  insurance executives and advocates for the poor told the
times  that thousands of new york children were wrongly placed in
the  program largely because participating insurance plans did not
steer  families into medicaid even when it was clear they belonged
there.

instruct  them to screen applicants for medicaid eligibility.
''the  department of health knew exactly what we were doing,''
said  michael a. stocker, president and chief executive of empire

enrolled  in the program. ''there is no secret about this. and there
is  no question that it is going to create problems.''

the  problems arose because time was needed to iron out the program.
''obviously  our top priority is to get children the health
insurance  they need and deserve,'' signor said. ''the federal
government  is now forcing states to move children who are eligible
for  medicaid into that program.'' he estimated that about 22
percent  of the children would have to be moved, but insurers and
others  put the figure closer to 50 percent.
state  comptroller carl mccall warned the health department
several  times over the last few years that it was enrolling too
many  children who belonged in medicaid, the newspaper said. the
department  responded to a 1998 audit by assuring mccall's office
that  it was requiring insurance carriers to screen applicants.
the  program was intended to insure children from low-income
families  whose incomes are too high for medicaid but too low to
afford  private insurance.
new  york, where the program is known as child health plus, is
one  of 10 states that have established a significant program so
far.  new york's enrolled children comprise roughly one quarter of
all  children in the program nationwide.
the  federal insurance program was approved by congress in 1997
and  is reimbursed by the federal government at a higher rate than
medicaid.  new york gets a 65 percent reimbursement, compared with
50  percent for medicaid.
the  federal government is examining whether new york state may
owe  it money, the times said.

[HEADLINE] :  carl sigman, songsmith who made generations hum, dead at 91
[TEXT]
	  manhasset, n.y. (ap) - carl sigman, who wrote music or words for
dozens  of songs, including the theme song to the 1950's ''robin
hood''  television series, died tuesday at age 91.
one  of sigman's best-known legacies is a phone number. in 1938
he  wrote ''pennsylvania 6-5000,'' in tribute to the hotel
pennsylvania,  where the dorsey brothers, benny goodman and artie
shaw  regularly performed. the glenn miller orchestra recorded the
song.  the phone number, pe6-5000, still rings at the hotel.
sigman  wrote the words to duke ellington's ''all too soon'' in
1940  and ''what now my love,'' for which he wrote english lyrics in
1966  for a french song written four years earlier. herb alpert and
the  tijuana brass, sonny and cher and mitch ryder sang his version.
he  also wrote the words to ''ebb tide,'' a song originally
composed  as an instrumental by the harpist robert maxwell; vic
damone,  the platters and the righteous brothers, among others,
recorded  it.
more  recently, his ''enjoy yourself'' was used in the 1997 woody
allen  movie ''everybody says i love you.''
sigman's  son, michael, noted that a mercedes commercial shown
during  the current olympics used ''enjoy yourself.''
a  graduate of new york university law school, sigman was
admitted  to the bar, but never practiced. instead, he was drawn to
music  and became acquainted with johnny mercer, the lyricist,
vocalist  and composer who became his mentor.
in  1942, sigman was drafted into the army and served in europe
in  the crew of a glider. he was awarded a bronze star for heroism.
he  also wrote what became the 82nd airborne division's official
song,  ''the all american soldier,'' receiving a $25 war bond for
the  achievement.

were  likely burned by the vandals of northern europe when they
plundered  olbia in the 5th century.
the  discovery ''is particularly important because it gives us
details  on a specific historical event'' as well as ancient naval
technology,  he said.
d'oriano  said another five ships from the 13th century were
found  in the same area, d'oriano said.
the  wreckage was found during work on an underwater tunnel at
the  port of olbia.
the  roman ships -- some up to 30 yards long -- are believed to be
merchant  vessels. the hulls show signs of fire.
so  far, the wreckage has yielded human bones, oil lamps, coins,
a  statue of the egyptian god osiris, a sapphire, an amphora and
fragments  of a bronze statue.
d'oriano  said divers are still exploring the wreckage.

[HEADLINE] :  hondurans search for helicopter
[TEXT]
tegucigalpa,  honduras (ap) -- honduran soldiers launched a search
friday  for a helicopter carrying the chief justice of the country's
supreme  court and five others which disappeared in bad weather.
the  bell-206 helicopter took off from islas de bahia, 180 miles
north  of the capital tegucigalpa, earlier friday and disappeared
from  radar screens shortly after, aviation authorities said.
tropical  storm keith is about 200 miles north of the coast, and
has  drenched northern honduras where the chopper disappeared with
heavy  rains.
honduran  air force officials said they would wait until saturday
to  launch an air search for the craft, but soldiers and police were
already  searching on the ground for judge oscar avila banegas and
the  five others.
besides  banegas, a congressman, the pilot, two court employees
and  banegas' bodyguard were on board. their names were not
immediately  available.
luis  rolando leiva, director of honduras' civil aviation agency,
said  ''the craft went down due to the prevailing bad weather.''

[HEADLINE] :  no injuries in madrid office blast
[TEXT]
madrid,  spain (ap) -- a bomb blamed on a leftist group exploded
saturday  at an office of the ruling popular party in madrid,
causing  minor damage and no injuries, said police.
a  police spokesman in madrid said a woman called police after
the  explosion to say grapo, an elusive group with apparent
anarchist  leanings, planted the bomb in the office in madrid's
hortaleza  neighborhood. nobody was in the building at the time of
the  explosion.
the  homemade bomb, with 3.3 pounds of explosive material, was
left  in the office doorway and a witness told police he saw two
young  men running from the scene shortly before the blast.
the  pre-dawn explosion was the fifth in three days blamed on
grapo.
 on  friday, two men and a woman planted a bomb in a trash bin in
the  barcelona office of el mundo, one of spain's leading
newspapers.  the building was evacuated. when the device exploded,
it  injured two police officers who had rushed to the scene.
on  wednesday, three bombs exploded at temporary employment
agencies  in three spanish provincial capitals, causing considerable
damage  but no injuries. grapo, which has targeted temporary job
offices  in the past, claimed all three.
grapo  has killed some 60 people in sporadic bombings and
shootings  since it emerged in the 1970s.
the  group has never stated clearly its political aims although
it  is believed to go after what it considers to be right-wing and
capitalist  targets.
its  name -- october first anti-fascist resistance group -- comes
from  october 1, 1975, the date of the group's first major attack in
which  it killed four policemen in reprisal for the execution of two
suspected  basque separatists and three anarchists belonging to
frap,  a predecessor group of grapo. the firing squad executions
were  the last by the regime of the late dictator gen. francisco
franco.

[HEADLINE] :  official: us hostage visited rebels
[TEXT]
jolo,  philippines (ap) -- an american being held hostage by
muslim  rebels visited their camp twice before being abducted and
discussed  procuring night vision goggles for them, the philippine
national  police chief said saturday.
jeffrey  schilling, of oakland, calif., was taken captive by the
abu  sayyaf rebels aug. 28 after he visited their camp on southern
jolo  island in sulu province. schilling says rebel leaders abducted
him  after they began suspecting he was a cia agent, which he
denies.
 but  national police chief panfilo lacson said schilling also had
visited  a rebel camp on the nearby province of basilan.
''twice  in the past two years schilling visited the abu sayyaf
camp  in basilan (and met) with abu sayyaf leaders for the
procurement  of night vision goggles,'' lacson said in an interview
with  abs-cbn television.
''because  he went there without any difficulty, we are wondering
why  he was kidnapped, because he went to sulu and transacted
business.''
 the  rebel faction holding schilling previously operated on
basilan,  but fled to jolo to escape a military assault after they
kidnapped  about 50 children and teachers from two schools.
on  sept. 16, the military launched a massive attack on jolo to
rescue  17 other hostages being held by the abu sayyaf, including
schilling  and three malaysians.
philippine  officials have raised questions about schilling's
relationship  with the rebels, although they say they continue to
believe  he is being held against his will.
schilling's  wife, ivi osani, is the second cousin of the abu
sayyaf's  spokesman and the widow of a rebel killed several years
ago  by government troops.
osani,  who went to the rebel camp with schilling but was not
abducted,  is being held by police.
schilling,  24, majored in near east studies at the university of
california  at berkeley and converted to islam in 1994. he is deeply
interested  in the status of muslim minorities in countries like the
philippines,  his family says.
the  abu sayyaf claims it is fighting for an independent islamic
state  in the impoverished southern philippines. in the past six
months  it has kidnapped scores of people. most were released after
libya  and malaysia paid more than $15 million in ransom,
negotiators  say.
several  philippine news reports have accused schilling of
discussing  procurement of supplies such as camouflage uniforms,
combat  boots and night vision goggles from the united states.
schilling's  mother, carol, has denied he was an arms dealer.
on  saturday, at least two rebels were killed and one soldier was
wounded  after a gunbattle erupted between government troops and
about  100 rebels in a mountainous area in patikul town, military
officials  said.

[HEADLINE] :  boxer de la hoya releasing album
[TEXT]
beverly  hills, calif. (ap) -- boxing hero oscar de la hoya says
he  has a soft side that nobody knows -- and he's ready to sing about
it.
 de  la hoya, 27, says he wants to retire from the ring in about
two  years and devote himself to music.
''i  want to do it forever,'' he said. ''i want to do it like
frank  sinatra.''
the  five-time world boxing champ and 1992 olympic gold medalist
is  releasing a self-titled album this month of love songs and
ballads.
 a  single, in which he sings the bee gees' hit ''run to me,'' has
been  released in english and spanish versions.
his  mother, a professional singer, dreamed of one of her sons
pursuing  a singing career, but de la hoya said he pursued his
father's  dream instead and became a fighter.
''it's  like somebody being trapped in somebody else's body.
that's  exactly the way i've been feeling,'' he said. ''and now with
my  singing, i can be the real me.''

[HEADLINE] :  colombians apologize to red cross
[TEXT]
bogota,  colombia (ap) -- in an unusual act of contrition,
right-wing  militias in colombia have apologized for dragging a
wounded  guerrilla from a red cross vehicle last week and executing
her.
 the  apology from the united self-defense forces of colombia, an
umbrella  group for the country's militias, was contained in a
letter  faxed to the red cross in bogota on thursday.
''we  accept our responsibility for this lamentable incident that
put  at risk the good work of the international red cross in
colombia,''  the letter said.
the  red cross had no comment on the apology.
in  its letter, the militia group conceded that on sept. 22 three
of  its fighters stopped a red cross vehicle outside apartado, a
town  near the panamanian border.
the  men then grabbed the wounded guerrilla, whom the red cross
was  taking to a hospital, and later killed her. she was a member of
the  leftist revolutionary armed forces of colombia, or farc, the
red  cross said.
apologies  are rare in colombia's brutal, 36-year civil war,
which  has left at least 35,000 people dead, most of them civilians.
[DOCNO] :  apw20000930.0068
[HEADLINE] :  gunfire erupts in jerusalem
[TEXT]
jerusalem  (ap) -- thousands of rock-throwing palestinian rioters
clashed  with israeli troops across the west bank, gaza strip and
jerusalem  on saturday, and gun battles raged in two areas in what
palestinians  said was a religious war over a bitterly contested
jerusalem  shrine.
in  a second day of bloody clashes, three palestinians, including
a  14-year-old boy, were killed in the west bank, while in gaza a
protester  was comatose with a bullet wound in the head, palestinian
doctors  said. about 325 palestinians were injured, hospital
officials  said.
''the  battle for jerusalem has begun,'' said bassem naim, a
palestinian  activist.
huge  plumes of black smoke from burning tires rose high above
palestinian  towns, and streets were littered with rocks and
overturned  garbage bins.
in  hebron, rioters running out of rocks had them ferried to the
scene  in taxis. helmeted israeli soldiers fired rubber-coated steel
pelles  and live rounds from behind jeeps and walls. gun battles
raged  near the west bank town of nablus and close to the jewish
settlement  of netzarim.
south  of nablus, about a dozen masked palestinians, crouching
behind  walls and olive trees, exchanged fire with israeli troops
for  more than an hour. two palestinians, including a 14-year-old
boy,  were killed in the clash, doctors said. in the west bank town
of  ramallah, a 16-year-old protester was killed, doctors said.
''the  israelis must understand that palestinians can also shoot
and  kill,'' said a 25-year-old gunman armed with an m-16 assault
rifle  who would not give his name.
near  netzarim, palestinian police in uniform and plainclothes
exchanged  fire with israeli troops.
palestinians  say the trigger for the violence was a visit
thursday  by israel's hawkish opposition leader, ariel sharon, to
the  disputed jerusalem hilltop known to jews as the temple mount
and  to muslims as haram as-sharif, or noble sanctuary. al aqsa is
one  of two major mosques in the walled compound.
in  clashes at the compound friday, six palestinians were killed
and  close to 200 wounded. ''we're going to teach them not to touch
our  holy place,'' said khalil natash, 21, a stone-thrower in the
west  bank town of hebron, who carried a black flag of mourning for
those  killed. ''we will burn the ground underneath the israelis to
stop  them from touching our holy place.''
israeli  prime minister ehud barak appealed to palestinian leader
yasser  arafat to restore calm. he said israel has been showing
''maximum  restraint,'' but would do what was necessary to protect
its  citizens and restore order. the violence erupted as israelis
marked  the jewish new year.
palestinian  peace negotiator nabil shaath said israeli security
forces  committed ''premeditated murder'' at the jerusalem shrine
friday.  the violence underscored palestinian demands that israel
must  withdraw from east jerusalem, the sector the palestinians
claim  as a future capital, shaath said.
marwan  barghouti, the fatah leader in the west bank, said he
expected  confrontations to intensify in the coming days.
''the  way the israelis are behaving now in the palestinian
territories  and israel's reluctance to express regret over what has
been  done at the mosque is encouraging the spread of the
confrontations,''  he said.
many  israelis felt the palestinians were responsible. ''despite
the  fact that there is a peace process, they (the palestinians)
want  to ruin everything,'' said meirav buchbut, 21, a bookkeeper
from  the town of netanya. ''there won't be peace. there will only
be  war.''
across  the west bank, gaza strip and east jerusalem,
palestinians  observed a general strike and day of mourning
saturday.  shops were closed and children were sent home from
school.  israel barred its citizens from entering the
palestinian-controlled  areas to avoid further friction.
israeli-palestinian  peace talks are hung up because of rival
sovereignty  claims to the shrine. neither side wants the other to
have  full control. all u.s. compromise proposals have been rejected
so  far by the negotiators.
in  visiting the shrine thursday, sharon, who staunchly opposes
concessions  to the palestinians, said he wanted to demonstrate that
israel  is in control there.
the  palestinians accused the israeli government of having
ignited  a ''religious war'' because it did not stop sharon from
visiting  the shrine.
jerusalem's  hawkish mayor, ehud olmert, a member of sharon's
likud  party, accused palestinian security forces of orchestrating
the  violence.
[DOCNO] :  apw20000930.0069
[HEADLINE] :  albright: milosevic is finished
[TEXT]
reykjavik,  iceland (ap) -- secretary of state madeleine albright
urged  russia on saturday to accept that slobodan milosevic was
''finished''  as president of yugoslavia.
albright  was reacting to news that russian president vladimir
putin  had offered to send foreign minister igor ivanov to belgrade
to  talk to both sides in yugoslavia's election standoff.
so  far, russia hasn't taken sides in the dispute over who won
yugoslavia's  presidential vote on sunday. opposition candidate
vojislav  kostunica says he beat president slobodan milosevic
outright,  while milosevic says a runoff is necessary to determine
the  winner because kostunica got less than 50 percent of the vote.
albright  said she planned to speak to ivanov later in the day,
and  would stress that kostunica had won the election.
''i  think the russians need to make clear that they understand
that  this has been a procedure where the opposition has won,''
albright  said at a news conference in reykjavik.
''the  russians need to understand that milosevic lost in this
round.  he is finished. it is time for him to go.''
albright  also said she had spoken to leading parties in the
middle  east peace process in an effort to ease tensions which
erupted  in violence in jerusalem.
she  said that she had telephoned both yasser arafat, the
palestinian  leader, and israel's prime minister ehud barak in a bid
to  keep the peace process on course.
''we  are very concerned about the violence. it is clearly
counterproductive  in the peace process,'' albright said. ''there is
danger  of a cycle of violence developing. the talks are at a very
delicate  stage and it is important that the violence stops.''
albright  stopped briefly in iceland, a nato ally, on her way to
france  and germany, and met with foreign minister halldor
asgrimsson  and prime minister david oddsson.
an  agreement between the two countries for the u.s. use of the
military  base at keflavik in southwest iceland is due for renewal
in  april. iceland relies on nato and the u.s. forces for its
defense.
 albright  said any changes in u.s. commitments to iceland were
unlikely.

[HEADLINE] :  6 palestinians killed in clashes
[TEXT]

several  gunmen clashed with israeli troops saturday in what
palestinians  said was a religious war over a bitterly contested
jerusalem  shrine. six palestinians were killed and about 325
injured  in the worst violence in the west bank and gaza strip in
four  years.
''the  battle for jerusalem has begun,'' said bassem naim, a
palestinian  activist.
palestinian  gunmen and israeli troops exchanged fire in two
locations,  near the jewish settlement of netzarim in gaza and south
of  the west bank town of nablus.
at  the netzarim junction, a palestinian fired shots at an
israeli  army outpost from behind a red truck. soldiers returned
fire,  and several palestinians took cover on the ground, covering
their  heads with their hands, their faces pressed on the asphalt.
one  palestinian man screamed in pain when he was shot in the knee.
paramedics  ran into the line of fire to drag him to safety.
shifa  hospital in gaza city reported three dead -- a 12-year-old
boy,  a palestinian policeman and an ambulance driver.
in  the west bank, three palestinians were killed by israeli
fire,  including a 14-year-old boy shot in the abdomen during a gun
battle  between a dozen masked gunmen and israeli soldiers. the
gunmen  crouched behind walls and olive trees as they took aim as
the  israelis.

and  kill,'' said a 25-year-old gunman armed with an m-16 assault
rifle  who would not give his name.

with  rocks and overturned garbage trash bins.

''maximum  restraint,'' but would do what was necessary to protect
its  citizens and restore order. the violence erupted as israelis
marked  the jewish new year.

forces  committed ''premeditated murder'' at the jerusalem shrine

its  citizens and restore order. the violence erupted as israelis
marked  the jewish new year.
palestinian  peace negotiator nabil shaath said israeli security
forces  committed ''premeditated murder'' at the jerusalem shrine
friday.  the violence underscored palestinian demands that israel
must  withdraw from east jerusalem, the sector the palestinians
claim  as a future capital, shaath said.
marwan  barghouti, the fatah leader in the west bank, said he
expected  confrontations to intensify in the coming days.
''the  way the israelis are behaving now in the palestinian
territories  and israel's reluctance to express regret over what has
been  done at the mosque is encouraging the spread of the
confrontations,''  he said.
many  israelis felt the palestinians were responsible. ''despite
the  fact that there is a peace process, they (the palestinians)
want  to ruin everything,'' said meirav buchbut, 21, a bookkeeper
from  the town of netanya. ''there won't be peace. there will only
be  war.''
across  the west bank, gaza strip and east jerusalem,
palestinians  observed a general strike and day of mourning
saturday.  shops were closed and children were sent home from
school.  israel barred its citizens from entering the
palestinian-controlled  areas to avoid further friction.
israeli-palestinian  peace talks are hung up because of rival
sovereignty  claims to the shrine. neither side wants the other to
have  full control. all u.s. compromise proposals have been rejected
so  far by the negotiators.

[HEADLINE] :  nj wines -- a well-kept secret
[TEXT]
shamong,  n.j. (ap) - the workers make their way down row after
row  of leafy green vines, snipping off dangling clusters of smooth,
plump,  deep blue grapes.
it's  harvest time in the vineyards, and this scene is being
repeated  in some of the world's prime wine growing areas - the
bordeaux  region of france, along germany's rhine river, in
california's  napa valley - and in new jersey.
new  jersey?
yes,  new jersey.
from  the rocky hills of warren county to the sandy cape may
county  coastal plain, there are 16 wineries turning out everything
from  merlots to chardonnays to cranberry, apple and blueberry
wines.
 in  fact, the garden state's $10 million-a-year wine industry
might  just be its best-kept agricultural secret.
''it's  an unknown quantity,'' said bill walker, marketing
specialist  at the state department of agriculture. ''ninety percent
of  the state's citizens don't even know that there is a wine
industry.''
 new  jerseyans are a thirsty bunch - the state ranks fifth in the
nation  in per capita wine consumption. but only 1 percent of what's
consumed  here is made in new jersey.
of  the 45 states that make wine, new jersey is among the top 15
in  output, producing about 1 million bottles of wine in 1999. but
wine  spectator magazine, considered by some vinophiles to be the
bible  of wines, has never even reviewed a new jersey wine.
not  because they're not good, magazine spokesman terrence meck
is  quick to point out, but because most of the wineries are too
small.
 ''for  a national publication, we're required to review wines
that  have a much larger, broader distribution,'' he said. ''new
jersey  is known for having a good wine industry, but it's too small
still.''
 that's  about to change. ten to 15 new wineries are expected to
open  in new jersey in the next five to seven years, said joseph
fiola,  a specialist in small fruit and viticulture for rutgers
cooperative  extension. and more people are planting vineyards to
sell  grapes to wineries.
fiola,  who helps the state's grape industry with research and
development,  said he gets several inquiries a week from people
interested  in getting started. some are entrepreneurs looking for a
new  venture; others are fruit farmers who want to diversify, he
said.
 many  of the newcomers want to plant in the southern part of the
state,  where the weather is perfect for the grapes that are in the
most  demand, fiola said.
most  of new jersey's wineries are in the hilly northern part of
the  state, which has cool weather and is good for growing such
grapes  as riesling and pinot noir. but the most popular grapes,
such  as cabernet sauvignon, cabernet franc, merlot and chardonnay,
require  a long, warm growing season. southern new jersey, with
moderating  winds from the delaware river, delaware bay and atlantic
ocean,  is much warmer than the north.
''i  think that'll make a big difference if we can get these
quality  grapes growing in south jersey,'' fiola said.
rather  than view the newcomers as competition, the state's
winemakers  say they welcome them.
''we've  got some exciting areas to grow grapes and a lot of
advantages  that people don't seem to be recognizing,'' said john
altmaier,  winemaker at unionville vineyards in ringoes.
altmaier,  who received the ''winemaker of the year'' award from
vineyard  and winery management magazine in 1998 and has worked in
vineyards  in germany and australia, acknowledged that the state has
a  ''reputation problem.''
''i  think that's a new jersey thing, and those things are hard
to  change,'' he said. ''but things are picking up.''
the  state's wines don't suffer image troubles in malaysia, japan
or  cuba, though. tomasello winery in hammonton exports its fruit
wines  to those countries and is working on distributing in iceland
and  europe, said marketing director lydia reese.
''our  fruit wines are made with 100 percent blueberries,
raspberries  and cranberries and have been very popular with the
asian  community,'' she said. ''one reason is they're very healthy,
with  very high antioxidants, and they have a unique flavor.''
tomasello,  which produced 38,000 cases last year, is one of the
larger  wineries in the state. most are small, family-run operations
that  don't have large marketing and distribution systems. they sell
most  of their wine at their wineries and rely on word-of-mouth,
newsletters  and wine festivals for publicity.
charles  beatty, wine director at canal's discount liquor mart in
marlton,  said new jersey wines ''can't compete with california or
french  wines'' and are viewed as more of a novelty.
''i  support the wineries because they are unique to new jersey.
you'll  never find blueberry wine anywhere else. i love them. i sell
them,''  he said, ''but how often do people drink blueberry wine?''
anthony  b. valenzano, who runs valenzano winery in shamong with
his  father and brother, said maybe people should stop comparing new
jersey  wineries to california's and should concentrate on what
grows  well here.
''california  has done a good job of convincing people that
cabernets,  chardonnays and merlots are the only good grapes, but
there  are other good grapes that make good wines,'' he said.
those  who taste new jersey wines for the first time generally
are  impressed, said altmaier.
''as  a winemaker, i'm not going to try to convince you that
they're  the greatest wines in the world. but there's not a flaw in
them.  they're nicely made. most people are surprised when they come
here.  they never knew new jersey had wines like this,'' he said.
on  the net: http://www.newjerseywines.com
[DOCNO] :  apw20000930.0075

[HEADLINE] :  hillary clinton seeks to energize black voters
[TEXT]
albany,  n.y. (ap) - hillary rodham clinton, trying to stitch
together  a coalition that will carry her to the u.s. senate, is
facing  a stiffer test in making sure blacks go the polls since new
york  city mayor rudolph giuliani left the race.
her  success at getting out the black vote could determine the
outcome  of what appears to be a very close race against her new
republican  rival, rick lazio, a congressman from long island who
has  not generated the sort of animosity within the black community
the  mayor did.
''with  giuliani in the race, there would have been an
avalanche''  of black votes for clinton, said state comptroller h.
carl  mccall, the only black ever elected to statewide office in new
york.
 ''the  difference is, we'll need a bigger effort to energize the
community,  but it will be energized on the basis of the issues that
hillary  clinton has been talking about and has been identified with
for  a long time,'' mccall, a democrat considering a run for
governor  in 2002, predicted.
but  there are some who are cautioning she must do more.
''we  all knew why we didn't want giuliani in the senate. with
giuliani  out, you've got to give us a reason to put you in the
senate,''  said the rev. al sharpton, a prominent figure in new
york's  black community, ''and i'm not sure that has been done.''
giuliani  has been heavily criticized for what critics say is a
lack  of sympathy to the needs of new york city's large minority
population  and being too supportive of a police force blacks have
viewed  as overly aggressive.
interestingly,  independent polls show that lazio, by the
numbers,  is no more a favorite with blacks than giuliani. but that
appears  more a function of clinton's popularity than anything lazio
has  done. a sept. 21 poll from marist college's institute for
public  opinion found clinton supported by 91 percent of black
voters.  a march poll from marist, taken when giuliani was still in
the  race, had her support at 87 percent among blacks.
the  mayor left the race in mid-may after learning he had
prostate  cancer.
what  the polls don't reflect is the political maxim that it is
easier  to get people to vote against something than for it.
''there  was little doubt the polarizing effect of giuliani would
have  put turnout of minorities off the charts,'' said marist
pollster  lee miringoff.
mccall  noted that the rev. jesse jackson made stops in syracuse
and  in new york city on monday and tuesday to help energize black
voters  and that san francisco mayor willie brown had also come to
help.
 ''i  am spending a good deal of my time trying to do that,''
mccall  added.
''we're  doing a lot of surrogate activity to get the drum beat
going,''  clinton campaign manager bill de blasio said.
the  first lady has also been visiting black churches - four in
queens  on sept. 17 alone and two in brooklyn the weekend before.
she  planned to visit four of them sunday in manhattan.
the  visits to the churches seemed to pay off judging by the
comments  of parishioners.
the  clintons ''were brought up the way we were brought up - to
treat  everyone fairly,'' said carol wilkins, of queens, who works
in  a housing project. ''i hope she makes it.''
''she'll  really work hard for us,'' said elsie murray, of
brooklyn,  who works for an insurance company. ''she loves people,
she's  sincere, she's not a phony.''
the  rev. henry simmons of st. albans congregational church in
queens  said clinton's visit there showed ''there's an earnest
desire  to hear from and to be with persons that are different and
whose  votes and whose support she knows she really needs.''
clinton  has also stepped up visits to minority neighborhoods and
interviews  with media outlets geared toward black and hispanic
communities,  de blasio said.
''we  are trying to insure that there are a series of elements
that  build up to the final turnout push,'' de blasio said.
she  and president clinton have courted black leaders from new
york  with overnight stays at the white house. mccall and his wife,
former  new york city deputy mayor joyce brown, stayed in the
lincoln  bedroom. the rev. floyd flake, a former congressman, and
manhattan  borough president c. virginia fields have also slept
over.
 clinton  aides are counting on the natural draw of a presidential
election,  plus phone banks and street volunteers to help offset any
falloff  in black interest because of giuliani's withdrawal.
they  are also counting on the popularity of the first lady, and
her  husband.
''the  motivational level is very high among people of color,
particularly  among women of color,'' de blasio said.
mccall  said there are plans to have president clinton ''speak to
targeted  groups in this state'' just before the election on his
wife's  behalf.
''you're  going to see president clinton in here with both
feet,''  maurice carroll, head of the quinnipiac university polling
institute,  predicted.
''the  bottom line is that people in communities of color relate
to  president clinton and if he is in the state, actively supporting
hillary,  they will duly note that and it will duly add to their
enthusiasm  for hillary,'' de blasio said.
while  de blasio and others have pointed with pride to a
get-out-the-vote  effort in 1998 in minority communities as being
instrumental  in helping elect democrats in new york, data shows
blacks  still tend to register and vote at a lower rate than whites.
while  about 17 percent of new york's voting age population is
black,  exit polling found that just 9 percent of voters in 1998
were  black.
sharpton  said that to energize black voters, clinton must speak
out  more forcefully on ''issues that resonate in our community,''
such  as racial profiling, police brutality and education.
''you  cannot be vague and nebulous and then expect a vote that
is  specific,'' he said.

[HEADLINE] :  atlantic city warehouse provides storage for pageant memorabilia
[TEXT]
atlantic  city, n.j. (ap) - when it was their turn, the
swimsuit-clad  contestants each stepped onto a giant wooden
turntable,  standing still as it turned them around for the judges
to  see.
when  the 1998 miss america pageant ended and the tv cameras went
off,  the turntable couldn't remain on the stage at convention hall.
it  had to go, but no one dared throw it out. after all, when you
stage  a live three-hour beauty pageant every year, you never know
what  props can be recycled for a future tv production number.
so  the turntable was shipped across town, to be stored amid
former  pageant stage sets, steel lighting trusses, souvenir
programs  and dozens of other pieces of not-ready-for-prime-time
equipment,  memorabilia and supplies belonging to the world's most
famous  beauty pageant.
''this  is the miss america warehouse,'' says manager bill weeks,
its  one and only employee. ''we have everything here, including the
kitchen  sink. two of them, in fact.''
the  warehouse, a nondescript two-story building made of blue
corrugated  metal, is located on kentucky avenue, about four blocks
from  convention hall.
unseen  by pageant contestants, tv viewers and news cameras, the
warehouse  becomes a hubbub of activity in the week before the
contestants  arrive here for the annual fall festivities and in the
days  after the new winner is crowned.
''with  different years, it's different things,'' said former
hostess  committee chairwoman mildred brick, 85, who led a reporter
and  photographer on a tour of the building recently.
''we  save a lot of stuff because whoever's doing the scene
designing  comes in here and sees what we have to start with. a lot
of  things get used over and over again,'' brick said.
dusty,  unmarked and barely recognizable from their appearances
on  stage, the old sets take up only a fraction of the space in the
building.
 most  of the rest is taken up by the plywood, mattresses,
mirrors,  shoe racks and assorted furniture needed to build the
pageant's  ''anchor station'' and a backstage area called ''sleepy
hollow,''  where exhausted tap dancers, pianists and baton twirlers
can  catch a few winks during rehearsals.
the  anchor station is a section of convention hall that is
converted  into the headquarters of miss america during the 12 days
between  their arrival and the telecast itself.
the  contestants sleep in casino hotel rooms and practice on
stage,  but every other activity is centered at the anchor station.
there,  they eat lunch, pose for photographs, sit for interviews
with  the press and gather before events. this is where the kitchen
sinks  come in: they are used for the food operation, which fixes
and  serves 5,000 meals to contestants, volunteers and pageant
hostesses  over the 12-day period.
the  plywood - which is stacked 15-feet high and 5-feet deep
against  a wall in the warehouse - is used to build the anchor
station  and an adjacent cluster of offices for pageant executives.
the  mattresses are kept in a climate-controlled room, to prevent
them  from mildewing. the mirrors - 55 oak-framed, 12-by-18-inch
vanity  mirrors - are covered in brown paper and stored just so, to
avoid  breakage.
''we  care for the girls from the minute they get here until the
minute  they leave. it's like setting up a whole home for them,
while  they're in atlantic city,'' brick said.
much  of what is stored in the warehouse is strictly archives. in
one  room, shelves are stacked with old copies of the miss america
program  book, a thick, glossy magazine-style publication listing
each  year's contestants, schedule of events and sponsors.
wrapped  in brown paper, labeled by winner - ''tawny godin,
1976''  - because each year's winner appears on the front cover of
the  following year's program. each package contains 100 copies of
that  year's program.
then  there are the dozen cardboard boxes packed with sheet
music,  most of it written by composer bernie wayne, the man who
penned  ''there she is,'' the song used to serenade the winner as
she  takes her runway walk.
like  any storage area, the miss america warehouse is a
hodgepodge  of old and new: walking through it, you see steel
lighting  trusses, 20-foot wooden pillars, stapled wooden risers,
gold  faux organ pipes, shoe racks and stacks of old correspondence.
''for  one or two days, we're here preparing and shipping stuff
and  then we're back here again after the pageant, because the stuff
has  to be out of convention hall,'' said brick.

[HEADLINE] :  thriller depicts n.korean soldiers
[TEXT]
seoul,  south korea (ap) -- wolves, monsters, baby-snatchers.
throughout  the cold war, the south korean government peddled
propaganda  about the denizens of its once-bitter foe, communist
north  korea.
now,  with reconciliation blooming on the korean peninsula,
southerners  are hungry to know what their old and mysterious enemy
is  really like.
they're  getting a warmer view at the cinema this month, where a
new  thriller depicts north korean soldiers as funny and vulnerable,
rather  than stereotypically cruel and inhuman.
since  it opened sept. 9, ''joint security area'' has drawn more
than  2 million viewers in a country of 47 million people and is
poised  to become south korea's biggest movie hit.
the  title of the tale about a murder investigation that
threatens  to topple the uneasy peace on the korean peninsula refers
to  the neutral border area in the demilitarized zone, or dmz. u.s.
soldiers  operate in the area, a negotiation site that has been the
scene  of confrontation and violence between the two sides on a few
rare  occasions.
dmz  jitters might wind down a notch soon. at their first-ever
talks  this week, the defense ministers of both koreas said their
soldiers  would cooperate in plans to reconnect a cross-border
railway.
 in  the movie, the lively portrayal of an illicit friendship
between  four south and north korean border guards matches the
curiosity  and yearnings of south koreans after five decades of
hostility.
 ''the  movie showed that ordinary citizens of north and south
korea  could mix together without any problem if it weren't for the
politics  and ideology that separates them,'' said kim yu-kyong, a
26-year-old  employee of an internet company.
tears  have been shed in a few theaters showing ''joint security
area,''  though far fewer than during a far more evocative, and
real-life,  event that helped humanize north koreans.
in  august, south koreans wept as they watched televised images
of  a round of anguished reunions of separated family members from
both  koreas who had not been able to meet in half a century.
the  reunions were the outcome of an unprecedented summit two
months  earlier between leaders of the koreas at which they agreed
to  work toward reunification, a goal expected to take years and
even  decades.
the  rapprochement has fueled south koreans' eagerness to learn
more  about their neighbors. books about the north are selling well,
television  stations show more programs about the north, and north
korea  studies are attracting more university students.
production  on ''joint security area'' began at a time when the
south's  attitude toward the north was softening under the aegis of
president  kim dae-jung and his policy of engaging pyongyang.
''the  north is viewed as the enemy,'' director park chan-wook
said.  ''i want to question whether that's really the right
perspective  on things.''
in  their roles as soldiers of opposing armies, his actors share
cigarettes,  arm wrestle, tell jokes and chat about girlfriends and
favorite  snacks. yet the shadow of the conflict that divided their
peninsula  at the end of world war ii is never distant, and violence
ensues.
 park's  movie departs from the dogmatic tradition of south korean
movies  in the 1960s and 1970s, when military-backed governments
urged  their citizens to trumpet the virtues of their system over
that  of the north.
last  year's homegrown hit, the spy thriller ''swiri'', injected
humanity  into inter-korean intrigue. the plot: a south korean
intelligence  agent falls in love with a north korean terrorist but
ends  up shooting her to death after discovering her true identity.
south  korea has been democratic for a decade, and filmmakers and
other  artists don't have to worry as much about violating
anti-communist  censorship laws that are no longer rigorously
enforced.
 the  penurious film industry in totalitarian north korea clings
to  its formulas.
in  a report last week, the north's foreign news outlet, kcna,
listed  movies such as ''star of korea'' and ''the sun of the
nation''  that glorify the achievements of kim il sung, the late
revered  leader and national founder.
''those  films, widely known as revolutionary ones, give the high
honor  and pride of the nation to the korean people who are
exceptionally  strong in the spirit of worshipping the leader,''
kcna  said.
